⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في استعمال المواضع المشتركة في الخاصة منها أنه إذا لم يكن الضد خاصة الضد الآخر فإنه إن لم يكن خاصة / العدل أنه أفضل شيء لم يكن خاصة الجور أنه أحسن شيء؛ وهذا يصلح للإثبات. ومنها ما يكون من المتضايفات مثل أنه إن لم يكن الفاصل خاصة الضعف فليس المفصول خاصة النصف؛ وإنه يصلح للإثبات والإبطال. ومنها ما يكون من العدم والملكة أنه إذا لم يكن عدم الحس خاصة للصمم لم يكن وجود الحس خاصة للسمع ; وإنه يصلح للإثبات والإبطال. ومنها ما يكون من المتناقضات بجهة أنه إن كان المحمول خاصة فمقابله بالنقيض ليست خاصة؛ وهذا للإبطال. ومنها ما يكون من جهة التقابل أيضًا وهو أنه إن كان الشيء خاصة للشيء فلا يكون خاصة لما يقابله بالنقيض؛ وإنه لا يصلح للإثبات إلا على سبيل المغالطة. ومنها ما يكون على سبيل تعادل القسمة من جنس واحد مثل أنه إن كان معقول ومحسوس وثابت وغير ثابت؛ ثم لم يكن الحيوان المحسوس خاصة للمائت لم يكن الحيوان المعقول خاصة لغير المائت نحو الملك. ومنها ما يكون من التصاريف أنه إذا كان المصروف ليس خاصة للمصروف؛ فليس التصريف خاصة للتصريف، وبالعكس؛ وهو موضع جدلي للإثبات والإبطال وتولده أمثلة مثل أنه إن لم يكن خاصة ما هو على طريق العدل أن يكون على طريقه الجميل لم يكن خاصة العدالة الجميل. وإن كان خاصة الإنسان أنه مشاء ذو رجلين كانت خاصة ما يجري على طريق الإنسانية أنه يجري على طريق هذا المشيء. وكذلك يعتبر جانب سلب التصريف مع سلب المصروف مثل ما ليس على طريق العدل وما ليس على طريق الجميل وغير العدل وغير الجميل، وكذلك العدم والملكة والمضاف والضد.
Chapter on using common topoi in property. Among them: if the opposite is not a property of the other opposite, then if justice is not a property of the best thing, injustice is not a property of the worst thing; this is suitable for affirmation. Among them is what comes from correlatives, like: if the divisor is not a property of the double, then the quotient is not a property of the half; it is suitable for affirmation and refutation. Among them is what comes from privation and possession: if absence of sense is not a property of deafness, then existence of sense is not a property of hearing; it is suitable for affirmation and refutation. Among them is what comes from contradictories in one respect: if a predicate is a property, then its contradictory opposite is not a property; this is for refutation. Among them is what comes from the direction of opposition also: that if a thing is a property of something, it is not a property of its contradictory opposite; it is not suitable for affirmation except by way of fallacy. Among them is what comes from equal division of one genus, like: if there is the intelligible and the sensible, the stable and the unstable; then if the sensible animal is not a property of the mortal, then the intelligible animal is not a property of the immortal, like the angel. Among them is what comes from inflections: if the inflected word is not a property of the inflected, then the inflection is not a property of the inflection, and vice versa; it is a dialectical topos for affirmation and refutation, and its examples are generated like: if it is not a property of what is on the way of justice that what is on the way of beauty is its property, then beauty is not a property of justice. And if man's property is that he is a walker with two legs, then the property of what runs on the way of humanity is that it runs on the way of this walking. And likewise the side of negation of inflection with negation of the inflected is considered, like what is not on the way of justice and what is not on the way of beauty, and non-justice and non-beauty, and similarly privation and possession, the relative, and the opposite.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a chapter listing common dialectical topoi (مواضع جدلية) used to establish or refute a property (خاصة). Each topos provides a rule based on a relation (opposition, correlation, etc.). The author first presents topoi from opposites: if one opposite is not a property of another opposite, then the other opposite is not a property of the first. Example: if justice is not a property of the best, then injustice is not a property of the worst. This works for affirmation (by contrapositive). Next, from correlatives (متضايفات): if the divisor is not a property of the double, then the quotient is not a property of the half. This works for both affirmation and refutation. Third, from privation and possession (عدم وملكة): if absence of sense is not a property of deafness, then presence of sense is not a property of hearing. Fourth, from contradictories (متناقضات): if a predicate is a property, its contradictory is not a property; this only refutes. Fifth, a variant of opposition: if something is a property of one thing, it is not a property of its contradictory; this is only valid for refutation, not affirmation (using it for affirmation is fallacious). Sixth, from equal division of a genus (تعادل القسمة): if a genus is divided into two species (e.g., animal into sensible and intelligible), then if one species is not a property of one member of the division, the other species is not a property of the other member (e.g., if sensible animal is not property of mortal, then intelligible animal is not property of immortal like angels). Seventh, from inflections (تصاريف): considering derived words (e.g., justice/just, beauty/beautiful). The rule: if the inflected form (e.g., 'just') is not a property of the base (e.g., 'justice'), then the inflection (e.g., 'justicehood') is not a property of the inflection (e.g., 'justness'), and vice versa. This topos is dialectical, for both affirmation and refutation. Examples are generated by transforming terms, such as: if what is on the way of justice does not have beauty as its property, then beauty is not a property of justice. Similarly, if man's property is 'walker with two legs', then what is on the way of humanity has the property of being on the way of this walking. The topos also considers the negative side: e.g., what is not on the way of justice, etc., and extends to privation/possession, relatives, and opposites.

Key Terms
تصاريف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only positive terms
B) Only negative terms
C) Both positive and negative sides
D) Neither positive nor negative sides

Key Takeaway
The inflectional topos allows property transfer between derived forms and their bases, with application to both positive and negative statements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the Arabic root 'ع-د-ل' (justice). The base is 'عدل' and the derived form is 'عادل' (just). Using the topos of inflections, construct an argument: if 'عادل' is not a property of 'عدل', then 'عدالة' (justicehood) is not a property of 'عدل'. Is this valid? Why?
?
Consider the negative side: 'non-justice' (لا عدل) and 'non-just' (لا عادل). Use the topos to argue about the relationship of properties. Provide an Islamic example in the context of divine justice.

Four Dialectical Topics for Testing Property
Author enumerates four dialectical topics using opposites, correlatives, privation, and contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four common dialectical topics (opposites, correlatives, privation/possession, contradictories) to test whether a predicate is a property (khassa) of a subject.

Core Idea
Four opposition relations provide dialectical tools to prove or refute property claims.

In dialectical argumentation, when testing whether something is a property (khassa) of another, the logicians identified four common topics based on opposition. These topics – opposites, correlatives, privation/possession, and contradictories – are wielded to either prove or refute a property claim. This lesson unpacks each topic with its corresponding logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of property (khassa)
First, recall that a property is a coextensive attribute that is not part of the essence. In dialectic, a property claim is a proposition linking a predicate to a subject. The topics help evaluate such claims.
Property is distinct from definition (hadd) and description (rasm).
2
Master the opposites topic (al-ḍiddān)
The rule for opposites: if one opposite (e.g., 'best') is not a property of a subject (e.g., 'justice'), then the other opposite ('worst') is not a property of the opposed subject ('injustice'). Form: If (P is not property of A), then (opposite of P is not property of opposite of A). This topic is used for proof (إثبات).
The text uses 'خاصة العدل أنه أفضل شيء' – 'property of justice that it is the best thing'.
3
Master the correlatives topic (al-mutaḍāyifāt)
For correlatives (e.g., double/half, part/whole): if the part is not a property of the double, then the whole is not a property of the half. Form: If (part is not property of double), then (whole is not property of half). This topic works for both proof and refutation.
Correlatives are pairs that necessarily implicate each other, like father and son.
4
Master the privation/possession topic (al-ʿadam wa al-milka)
For privation and possession (e.g., absence/presence of sensation): if the absence is not a property of deafness, then the presence is not a property of hearing. Form: If (absence of X is not property of A), then (presence of X is not property of B). Also usable for both proof and refutation.
Privation is the absence of a possession in a subject naturally capable of it.
5
Master the contradictories topic (al-mutanāqiḍāt)
For contradictories: if a predicate is a property of a subject, then its contradictory is not a property of that subject. This topic is only for refutation (إبطال). Form: If (P is property of S), then (not-P is not property of S).
Contradictories are pairs that cannot both be true or both false, like 'property' vs 'not property'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في استعمال المواضع المشتركة في الخاصة
منها أنه إذا لم يكن الضد خاصة الضد الآخر فإنه إن لم يكن خاصة العدل أنه أفضل شيء لم يكن خاصة الجور أنه أحسن شيء؛ وهذا يصلح للإثبات. ومنها ما يكون من المتضايفات مثل أنه إن لم يكن الفاصل خاصة الضعف فليس المفصول خاصة النصف؛ وإنه يصلح للإثبات والإبطال. ومنها ما يكون من العدم والملكة أنه إذا لم يكن عدم الحس خاصة للصمم لم يكن وجود الحس خاصة للسمع ; وإنه يصلح للإثبات والإبطال. ومنها ما يكون من المتناقضات بجهة أنه إن كان المحمول خاصة فمقابله بالنقيض ليست خاصة؛ وهذا للإبطال.
Chapter on the use of common topics concerning property.
Among them: if the opposite is not a property of the other opposite — for if it is not a property of justice that it is the best thing, then it is not a property of injustice that it is the worst thing; this is suitable for proof.
Among them is what concerns correlatives: if the part is not a property of the double, then the whole is not a property of the half; it is suitable for proof and refutation.
Among them is what concerns privation and possession: if absence of sensation is not a property of deafness, then presence of sensation is not a property of hearing; it is suitable for proof and refutation.
Among them is what concerns contradictories: if the predicate is a property, then its contradictory is not a property; this is for refutation.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a definitional enumeration of common dialectical topics used to test whether something is a property (خاصة) of something else. The author lists four types of opposition relations. The first uses opposites: if one opposite is not a property, the other is not either. The second uses correlatives: if a part is not a property, its whole is not. The third uses privation/possession: if absence is not a property, then presence is not. The fourth uses contradictories: if a predicate is a property, its contradictory is not. For each, the author indicates whether the topic is useful for proof (إثبات), refutation (إبطال), or both. These are dialectical tools, not demonstrative proofs.

المواضع المشتركة
الضدان
المتضايفات
العدم والملكة
المتناقضات

Key Takeaway
Four opposition-based topics – opposites, correlatives, privation/possession, and contradictories – provide dialectical tools for testing property claims in argumentation.

Opposition and Equality of Division Topics
Author introduces two dialectical topics: opposition and equality of division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the dialectical topics of opposition and equality of division to identify fallacious arguments and generate valid dialectical moves.

Core Idea
Opposition blocks property transfer; equality of division extends property across species.

This lesson covers two dialectical topics: opposition and equality of division. These tools are used in dialectical debate to either prove or refute claims by transferring properties from one thing to its opposite or across a divided genus. Understanding these will sharpen your critical thinking in Islamic argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property claim
Find the statement where a property is attributed to a thing. For example, 'knowledge is a property of the eternal'.
Property (خاصة) is a defining characteristic.
2
Check for opposition relation
Determine if the object in question has a contradictory opposite. If so, the opposition topic applies: the property cannot be transferred to the opposite.
Contradictory opposites are like eternal vs. created.
3
Apply the opposition rule
If property P belongs to X, then P does not belong to the contradictory of X. Using such an opposition to prove a claim is fallacious.
The rule only works for negation; it cannot be used affirmatively.
4
Identify the genus and its divisions for equality of division
Find a genus that is divided into mutually exclusive species. For example, 'animal' divided into 'rational' and 'sensible'.
The division must be exhaustive and exclusive.
5
Transfer the property across the division
If a property does not hold for one species, it does not hold for the opposite species within the same genus. In the example, if sensible animal is not a property of mortal, then rational animal is not a property of non-mortal.
The property is inverted along with the species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها ما يكون من جهة التقابل أيضًا وهو أنه إن كان الشيء خاصة للشيء فلا يكون خاصة لما يقابله بالنقيض؛ وإنه لا يصلح للإثبات إلا على سبيل المغالطة. ومنها ما يكون على سبيل تعادل القسمة من جنس واحد مثل أنه إن كان معقول ومحسوس وثابت وغير ثابت؛ ثم لم يكن الحيوان المحسوس خاصة للمائت لم يكن الحيوان المعقول خاصة لغير المائت نحو الملك. ومنها ما يكون من التصاريف أنه إذا كان المصروف ليس خاصة للمصروف؛ فليس التصريف خاصة للتصريف، وبالعكس؛ وهو موضع جدلي للإثبات والإبطال وتولده أمثلة مثل أنه إن لم يكن خاصة ما هو على طريق العدل أن يكون على طريقه الجميل لم يكن خاصة العدالة الجميل. وإن كان خاصة الإنسان أنه مشاء ذو رجلين كانت خاصة ما يجري على طريق الإنسانية أنه يجري على طريق هذا المشيء. وكذلك يعتبر جانب سلب التصريف مع سلب المصروف مثل ما ليس على طريق العدل وما ليس على طريق الجميل وغير العدل وغير الجميل، وكذلك العدم والملكة والمضاف والضد.
وفي موضع التصاريف والنظائر نظر علمي وهو أنه ليس يجب إذا كان المشتق خاصة المشتق أن يكون المصدر خاصة للمصدر بل ربما لم يكن المصدر محمولا على المصدر مثلا إذا كان الضاحك خاصة للناطق يكون الضحك خاصة النطق حتى يقال إن النطق ضحك وإن كان الضحك محمول عليه مساو له. وأما إذا كان الضحك خاصة النطق كان الضحاك خاصة الناطق لا محالة. ومع ذلك لا يحمل المصدر على المصدر.
And among them is what concerns also the aspect of opposition: if a thing is a property of something, then it is not a property of its contradictory opposite; and it is not suitable for proof except by way of fallacy.
And among them is what concerns equality of division within a single genus: for example, if there is rational and sensible, fixed and non-fixed; then if the sensible animal is not a property of the mortal, then the rational animal is not a property of the non-mortal, like an angel.
And among them is what concerns derivatives: if the conjugated word is not a property of the base word, then the conjugation is not a property of the conjugation, and vice versa; it is a dialectical topic for proof and refutation, and examples are generated such that if it is not a property of what is on the path of justice to be on its path of beauty, then it is not a property of justice beauty. And if being a walker with two legs is a property of man, then being on the path of humanity is a property of what proceeds on the path of this walking. Likewise, the aspect of negating the conjugation with the negation of the base is considered, such as what is not on the path of justice and what is not on the path of beauty, and other-than-justice and other-than-beauty, and similarly privation and possession, correlative, and opposite.
And in the topic of derivatives and parallels there is a scientific consideration: it is not necessary that if the derived term is a property of the derived-from, then the source is a property of the source; rather, perhaps the source is not predicated on the source. For example, if 'laughing' (dahik) is a property of 'speaking' (natiq), then 'laughter' (dahk) is a property of 'speech' (nutq), such that it is said that speech is laughter, even if laughter is predicated on it equally. But if laughter is a property of speech, then laughing is necessarily a property of the speaker. Nonetheless, the source is not predicated on the source.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage presents three more dialectical topics and then critically refines the third. The first topic warns that using contradictory opposites for proof can lead to fallacy. The second uses equality of division within a genus to transfer property between species and their opposites. The third concerns derivatives: if a derived term is not a property of its base, then the derivational pattern is not a property of the base pattern, and vice versa. However, the author then adds a critical note (نظر علمي) pointing out that the relation is not symmetrical: a derived term being a property of its base does not guarantee the source term is a property of the source. He gives the example of 'laughing' and 'speaking'. This refinement is essential to avoid a false inference.

تقابل
تعادل القسمة

Key Takeaway
The opposition topic prevents contradictory properties from being ascribed to opposites, while equality of division allows property transfer across exclusive species of a genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Derivative Topic and Its Critical Refinement
Author presents the derivative topic and then critically refines it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which property transfer between derived terms and their sources is valid and avoid the fallacy of assuming symmetry.

Core Idea
Derived-property relation is not reversible; the critical note refines the rule.

The third dialectical topic concerns derivatives: how properties transfer between a derived word and its base. The author first states the rule, but then adds a critical scientific note that this rule is not always symmetric. This lesson examines both the rule and its refinement, showing the importance of nuanced logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Understand the derivative rule
The initial rule: if the derived word (e.g., 'laughing') is not a property of the base word (e.g., 'laughter'), then the derivational pattern is not a property of the base pattern, and vice versa.
This is a dialectical topic for both proof and refutation.
2
Recognize the bidirectional claim
The rule is stated as symmetric: if P not property of Q, then the pattern of P is not property of pattern of Q, and conversely. The text says 'and vice versa'.
Many examples follow, like the justice/beauty example.
3
Identify the critical refinement
The author then presents a 'scientific consideration': it is not necessary that if the derived term is a property of the derived-from, then the source is a property of the source in the same way.
The example of 'laughing' and 'speaking' illustrates the asymmetry.
4
Work through the example
If 'laughing' (dahik) is a property of 'speaking' (natiq), then 'laughter' (dahk) is a property of 'speech' (nutq). So the rule works from derived to source. But it does not follow that 'speech' is a property of 'laughter'.
The source (masdar) is not predicated on the source in reverse.
5
Apply the critical rule
When using the derivative topic, always check directionality. The property transfer from derived term to base works, but the reverse is not guaranteed. This prevents false analogies.
Use the critical note to refine your dialectical moves.

And among them is what concerns also the aspect of opposition: if a thing is a property of something, then it is not a property of its contradictory opposite; and it is not suitable for proof except by way of fallacy.
And among them is what concerns equality of division within a single genus: for example, if there is rational and sensible, fixed and non-fixed; then if the sensible animal is not a property of the mortal, then the rational animal is not a property of the non-mortal, like an angel.
And among them is what concerns derivatives: if the conjugated word is not a property of the base word, then the conjugation is not a property of the conjugation, and vice versa; it is a dialectical topic for proof and refutation, and examples are generated such that if it is not a property of what is on the path of justice to be on its path of beauty, then it is not a property of justice beauty. And if being a walker with two legs is a property of man, then being on the path of humanity is a property of what proceeds on the path of this walking. Likewise, the aspect of negating the conjugation with the negation of the base is considered, such as what is not on the path of justice and what is not on the path of beauty, and other-than-justice and other-than-beauty, and similarly privation and possession, correlative, and opposite.
And in the topic of derivatives and parallels there is a scientific consideration: it is not necessary that if the derived term is a property of the derived-from, then the source is a property of the source; rather, perhaps the source is not predicated on the source. For example, if 'laughing' (dahik) is a property of 'speaking' (natiq), then 'laughter' (dahk) is a property of 'speech' (nutq), such that it is said that speech is laughter, even if laughter is predicated on it equally. But if laughter is a property of speech, then laughing is necessarily a property of the speaker. Nonetheless, the source is not predicated on the source.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage presents three more dialectical topics and then critically refines the third. The first topic warns that using contradictory opposites for proof can lead to fallacy. The second uses equality of division within a genus to transfer property between species and their opposites. The third concerns derivatives: if a derived term is not a property of its base, then the derivational pattern is not a property of the base pattern, and vice versa. However, the author then adds a critical note (نظر علمي) pointing out that the relation is not symmetrical: a derived term being a property of its base does not guarantee the source term is a property of the source. He gives the example of 'laughing' and 'speaking'. This refinement is essential to avoid a false inference.

Key Terms
تصاريف
مشتق
مصدر
نظر علمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the critical note, if 'laughing' is a property of 'speaking', what follows?
A) 'Laughter' is necessarily a property of 'speech'.
B) 'Speech' is not a property of 'laughter'.
C) The source is predicated on the source.
D) The relation is symmetrical.

Key Takeaway
The derivative topic is a powerful dialectical tool, but its application requires careful attention to directionality; a derived term being a property of its base does not guarantee the reverse in all respects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the term 'alim (knowing) derived from 'ilm (knowledge). If 'knowing' is a property of 'God', does it follow that 'knowledge' is a property of 'God'? Apply the critical note to determine whether the predication holds symmetrically.
?
In a debate, an opponent argues: 'Since justice is not a property of the unjust, then being on the path of justice is not a property of being on the path of injustice.' Use the derivative topic to assess whether this argument is valid, and then apply the critical refinement to check for hidden asymmetry.

Proportion Topic for Property Transfer
Author introduces the proportion topic for property transfer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the proportion topic to transfer a property from one relatum to another in a dialectical argument.

Core Idea
Proportion between relations can transfer property from one relatum to another.

Dialectical argument often uses analogy between relations. The proportion topic allows you to transfer a known property from one pair of terms to another when the relations are analogous. This tool is critical for extending rulings or attributes in theological and legal debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the analogous relations
Find two pairs of things where the relation between the first pair is said to be like the relation between the second pair. Example: patient:health :: physician:health – the relation of receiving health vs giving health.
2
Determine the property in the first pair
The second term (e.g., health) is a property or not. If it is a property (khassa) of the first term (patient), then the corresponding term in the second pair (physician) will have a similar property.
The property must be genuine, not accidental.
3
Transfer the property to the second pair
If health is a property of the patient, then health (or a related property) is a property of the physician – but vice versa works too. The transfer is symmetric.
This is a topoi for dialectical inference.
4
Test with an Islamic example
In Kalam, the relation of Creator to creation is like the relation of artisan to artifact. If it is a property of the artisan to know his artifact, then it is a property of the Creator to know creation. Check if the analogy holds.
Ensure the property attaches from the species-aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المواضع ما يكون من النسبة وهو أنه إذا كانت نسبة شيء إلى شيء آخر كنسبة ثالث إلى رابع والثاني خاصة أو ليست بخاصة فالرابع خاصة أو ليست بخاصة مثلا إذا كان المرتاض نسبة إلى الحصيب نسبة الطبيب إلى الصحة؛ فإن كانت خاصة المرتاض أن يكون مفيدا للحصيب فخاصة الطبيب أن يكون مفيدا للصحة، وبالعكس. ومن المواضع ما يكون للإثبات والإبطال أنه ينبغي أن تكون الخاصة من المعاني اللاحقة للشيء من جهة نوعه، ويكون لنوعه بما هو نوعه؛ وبالجملة لماهياته ومن طريق ماهيته. وقد علمت معنى اللاحق من قبل فإنه إن كانت المادة خاصة ليست تلحقه من حيث هو هو كما يلحق السكونُ الإنسان من حيث صورته وماهيته بل من حيث هو جسم، أو كان يلحقه لكن لا من جهة تصير بها مساوية مثل اللاحقة التي هي من اللواحق للصورة الإنسانية ولكن ليست بخاصته حقیقته؛ فلا تكون الخاصة خاصة. وأما إذا كانت الخاصة مثل ما للحيوان من كونه مركبا من جسم ونفس فذلك يلحقه لطباعه وينعكس عليه؛ فهذه الخاصة جيدة لكن لقائل أن يقول إن كون الحيوان مركبا من جسم ونفس هو حده لا خاصته. فنقول إن المركب ليس من المعاني الجنسية للحيوان بل هو من لوازم جنسه بل جنس الجسم وفصله
(۱) النسخة كان وما أثبتناه هو الصواب كما هو الظاهر من السياق.
And among the topics is what concerns proportion: if the relation of something to something else is like the relation of a third to a fourth, and the second is a property or not a property, then the fourth is a property or not a property. For example, if the relation of the patient to health is like the relation of the physician to health; if it is a property of the patient to benefit from health, then it is a property of the physician to benefit health, and vice versa.
And among the topics for proof and refutation is that the property should be among the meanings that attach to the thing from the aspect of its species, and it is for its species qua species; in sum, for its quiddity and from the way of its quiddity. You have already learned the meaning of 'attaching' (lahiq). For if the matter is a property that does not attach to it insofar as it is itself — as stillness attaches to man from the aspect of his form and quiddity, but rather from the aspect that he is a body — or if it attaches to him but not from the aspect that makes it coextensive, like the accident that is among the accidents of the human form but is not a property of his reality, then it is not a property. But if the property is like what is for animal of being composed of body and soul, that attaches to it by its nature and is convertible; this property is good. However, one may object that the animal's being composed of body and soul is its definition, not its property. We reply: the composite is not among the generic meanings of animal but rather among the necessary concomitants of its genus, rather the genus of body and its differentia.
(1) The copy read 'was' and what we have established is correct, as is apparent from the context.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage presents two more topics and a key condition for property. The first topic uses proportion: if the relation between two things is analogous to another relation, property attribution can be transferred. For example, the patient's relation to health parallels the physician's relation to health. The second topic sets a normative condition: a true property must attach to the thing from its species-aspect (جهة نوعه), not accidentally. The author distinguishes between accidental predicates and genuine properties that are convertible. He then addresses a potential objection: if being composed of body and soul is the definition of animal, it cannot be its property. The reply clarifies that the composite is not a genus meaning but a necessary concomitant of the genus, thus it can be a property.

نسبة
خاصة

In the example from the passage, if 'health' is a property of the patient, what follows about the physician?
A) The physician also has health as a property.
B) The physician must be healthy.
C) The physician's relation to health is reversed.
D) Nothing can be concluded.

Key Takeaway
The proportion topic allows property transfer when two relations are analogous, but the property must be genuine and the analogy valid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a proportion argument in fiqh: If the relation of wine to intoxication is like the relation of khamr to intoxication, and khamr is prohibited due to intoxication, then wine is prohibited. Check if the property transfers validly.
?
Identify a proportion topic in a hadith argument: The Prophet said, 'The example of the one who recites the Quran is like the example of the citron...' (Bukhari). Explain how the property of the citron transfers to the reciter.

Conditions for a Genuine Property in Dialectics
Author explains conditions for a genuine property and addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a genuine property and an accidental attribute using the species-aspect condition and the objection-response about definition vs. property.

Core Idea
A genuine property must attach from the species-aspect and be convertible; it is a necessary concomitant of the genus, not the essence.

Not every attribute that accompanies a thing is a true property. The author sets a strict condition: a property must attach to the thing from its species-aspect, not from a higher genus. He also addresses a common objection: what seems like a definition may actually be a property if it is a concomitant of the genus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the candidate property (lāḥiq)
Look at the attribute that is claimed to be a property. In the passage, 'being composed of body and soul' is claimed for animal.
2
Determine the aspect of attachment
Does the attribute attach to the thing from its species-aspect (from its quiddity qua species) or from a higher genus? For example, stillness attaches to man from the aspect of being a body, not from being human, so it is not a genuine property of man.
The species-aspect means the attribute must be coextensive with the species.
3
Check convertibility (inʿikās)
A genuine property is convertible: if the thing has the property, and having the property implies the thing. For animal, being composed of body and soul is convertible – every animal is composed of body and soul, and whatever is composed of body and soul is an animal? Actually, the author says it 'attaches by its nature and is convertible.' So it passes.
Convertibility tests coextensiveness.
4
Resolve the definition objection
If someone objects that the attribute is a definition (had), not a property (khassa), the author replies that the composite is not a genus meaning but a necessary concomitant (lāzim) of the genus. So it can be a property even if it resembles a definition in being essential.
This distinction hinges on whether the attribute is part of the essence or a necessary consequence.

Crafting a Sound Dialectical Definition
Author lists requirements for a valid dialectical definition including avoid obfuscation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify flaws in a dialectical definition and propose corrections using the criteria of good formulation (sigha).

Core Idea
A dialectical definition needs clear wording, not deep ontological accuracy.

In dialectical debates, definitions are tools for persuasion rather than precise scientific analysis. This lesson explains how to craft a dialectical definition that is acceptable in jadal by focusing on clear formulation and avoiding common pitfalls. The author contrasts scientific and dialectical definitions, then lists the defects that render a definition invalid in a dialectical context.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish scientific from dialectical definitions
Notice that the author says dialectical definitions do not require the genus and differentia to be real (haqiqi); they can be mashhur (well-known). This relaxes the precision needed in scientific definitions.
This means that in dialectic, a definition can be based on common understanding even if it does not capture the true essence.
2
Identify the requirement of good sigha
The author stresses that the formulation (sigha) must be a 'good craft' (sana'a jayyida). If it is not, the definition is open to rejection (man').
Sigha refers to the phrasing and arrangement of genus and differentia in the definition.
3
Recognize the listed defects in sigha
The author lists: obscurity (ighlaq), including unnecessary elements, distorting the proper order of genus and differentia, and using metaphorical (musta'ar), figurative (majaz), ambiguous (mushtarak), or unfamiliar (gharib) language.
These defects make the definition unclear or misleading, which defeats the purpose of dialectical persuasion.
4
Apply these criteria to a sample definition
Take a dialectical definition such as 'Worship is humility before God'. Check if it uses a mashhur genus (humility) and a clear differentia. Then evaluate its sigha: is the wording clear? Does it contain any of the listed defects?
If the definition uses metaphorical language like 'servitude' without clarification, it may be rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول يمكن أن يكون مساويًا بحسب العموم، ولا يكون مساويًا بحسب المعنى المعتبر هو المساواة بحسب المعنى. وإنه لا يكون مساويًا بحسب المعنى إلا وأن يكون مساويًا بحسب العموم لكن هذا التحقيق لا يراعى في الحدود الجدلية؛ وينفع فيها بما يكون إلحاق الفصل فيه بجعل القول منعكسا على الحدود بل قد ينفع الجدلي بما هو دون هذا فإنه إن لم يكن الجنس ولا الفصل جنسًا حقيقيًا بل كان الجنس جنسا بحسب المشهور، والفصل فصلا كذلك كان الحد حدا عند الجدلي. فيجب أن تكون الصيغة الحاصلة من إيراد الجنس والفصل صنعة جيدة فإنها إذا لم تكن جيدة كان في حيز المنع. والوجوه التي بها يكون الحد غير جيد الصيغة هي مثل إغلاق اللفظ، وإدخال ما لا ينبغي، وتحريف ما ينبغي نحو الجنس والفصل عن جهة ما ينبغي، واستعمال اللفظ المستعار والمجاز والمشترك والغريب الوحشي مثلا؛ فإنه إذا كان كذلك فلا يكون الحد على ما ينبغي. وأما أنه كيف يكون حتى يكون حدا علميًا، أو حدا جدليًّا فقد مرَّ من قبل ما يعين على ذلك. وأما المواضع التي بعدها فمنها ما إذا أخذ بدل الجنس شيء من المحمولات العامة أو شيء من اللوازم التي يلزم كل شيء كالموجود والشيء وغير ذلك من الأسماء المشتركة أو المترادفة. وبالجملة ما لا يدل على أصل ماهية مخصوصة أو ما يدل عليه وعلى الزائد كذلك. وأما المواضع الخاصة بإثبات الحد وإبطاله.
Then the expression may be co-extensive in terms of generality, without being co-extensive in terms of meaning; the considered equality is equality in meaning. And it is not co-extensive in meaning unless it is co-extensive in terms of generality, but this verification (tahqiq) is not observed in dialectical definitions; benefit is taken in them from what attaches the differentia by making the expression convertible upon the definitions. Rather, the dialectician may benefit from something less than this: if the genus and the differentia are not real genus and differentia, but the genus is a genus according to what is well-known (mashhur), and the differentia similarly, then the definition is a definition in the eyes of the dialectician. So it is necessary that the form (sigha) resulting from adducing the genus and differentia be a good craft (sana'a jayyida); for if it is not good, it falls within the purview of rejection (man'). The ways in which the definition is not in good form are like: obscurity of wording (ighlaq al-lafz), including what should not be included, distorting what should be as regards the genus and differentia from the proper direction, using metaphorical language (musta'ar), figurative (majaz), ambiguous (mushtarak), and unfamiliar barbaric (gharib wahshiyya) etc. So if it is such, then the definition is not as it should be. As for how it should be to be a scientific definition or a dialectical definition, what guides to that has already passed. And as for the topics that follow: among them is when something from the general predicates (al-mahmulat al-'amma) is taken instead of the genus, or something from the concomitants (lawa'iz) that accompany everything, like 'existent' (mawjud) and 'thing' (shay') and other synonymous or homonymous names. In general, what does not indicate the foundation of a specific quiddity, or what indicates it and something additional as well. And as for the special topics of proving and refuting a definition.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage discusses dialectical definitions (hudud jadaliyya). The author begins by making a distinction: an expression may be co-extensive in generality (i.e., applies to all individuals of the definiendum) but not co-extensive in meaning (i.e., it may not capture the essence). For scientific definitions, this is not acceptable; but in dialectic, the focus is on the form and persuasion, not on deep verification. Therefore, dialectical definitions often use popular (mashhur) genera and differentiate rather than the real, essential ones. The key condition for a good dialectical definition is that its formulation (sigha) must be 'crafted well' (sana'a jayyida). The author then lists the defects that make a definition poorly formulated: 1) obscurity (ighlaq) of wording, 2) including what should not be included, 3) distorting what should be included (e.g., misplacing genus and differentia), 4) using metaphorical language (musta'ar), figurative speech (majaz), ambiguous terms (mushtarak), or unfamiliar barbarisms (gharib wahshiyya). If any of these occur, the definition is not acceptable in dialectic either. The author then mentions that the topics that follow include cases where one takes a general predicate (like 'existent' or 'thing') as a substitute for the genus, or a concomitant (lazim) that is always present. These are also problematic because they fail to indicate the specific foundation of the quiddity or they include additional elements. The passage ends by noting that there are specific topics for proving and refuting definitions. Overall, this lesson provides practical guidelines for constructing dialectical definitions that are persuasive without being overly strict.

Key Terms
الصيغة (al-sigha): The formulation or phrasing of a definition; the way genus and differentia are expressed. [Note: In logic, sigha often refers to the form of a proposition or definition.]
المشهور (al-mashhur): Well-known or commonly accepted — used in dialectic as a basis for premises. [Note: One of the types of premises in the five arts; also used in usul al-fiqh.]
المحمولات العامة (al-mahmulat al-'amma): General predicates — like 'existent', 'thing', 'one', etc., which apply to many different quiddities. [Note: These are often used in metaphysical discussions; in definition, they are too broad.]
المنع (al-man'): Rejection — a dialectical move denying the validity of a definition or argument. [Note: In jadal, man' is one of the standard objections.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is listed as a defect that makes a dialectical definition unacceptable?
A) Using a well-known genus instead of a real genus.
B) Using the term 'existent' as a general predicate.
C) Using metaphorical language (musta'ar).
D) Using a concomitant (lazim).

Key Takeaway
A good dialectical definition requires clear, precise phrasing (sigha) free from obscurity, metaphor, ambiguity, or unnecessary additions, even if it relies on well-known (mashhur) terms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Consider the dialectical definition 'Khabar al-Wahid is a report transmitted by a single chain of narrators'. Identify any potential defects in its sigha according to the passage (e.g., is the term 'report' ambiguous? Does it include unnecessary elements?).
?
Task 2: Construct a dialectical definition for 'analogy' (qiyas) in usul al-fiqh. Then evaluate your definition against the defects listed in the passage. Write a brief objection (man') based on one of the defects, and a response (jawab) that attempts to fix it.

5 min
The Locus of Convertibility (al-Tasrif)
Locus of convertibility for proving identity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to use the locus of convertibility to test whether two attributes are essentially identical in a dialectical argument.

Core Idea
Convertibility: if two attributes are identical, their predicates are interchangeable.

In dialectical debates, one common strategy to prove the identity of two things is to check whether their predicates are convertible. If the attributes are essentially the same, then the terms apply to the same subject and can be swapped. This locus, called al-tasrif, is foundational for distinguishing essential identity from accidental predication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two attributes
Find the two attributes being compared in the passage. The example uses justice and courage.
2
Check convertibility
Verify if the predicate of one can be applied to the subject of the other. The passage states: 'the courageous person is just, and the just person is courageous'.
This is the core test of identity.
3
Distinguish from accidental predication
Note that for accidental attributes, convertibility is not required—only predication holds. This is the key differentiator.
Accident does not imply هو هو (itselfness).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من المواضع مواضع التصريف كما إذا كانت العدالة بعينها الشجاعة؛ فالشجاع عدل، والعدل شجاع، وبالعكس إن كان العدل هو بعينه الشجاع. فالشجاعة عدالة، والعدالة شجاعة ويخالف المواضع في باب العرض فإنه لا يجب هناك الهو هو بل هناك حمل فقط . وكذلك في المتقابلات والفاسدات والأسباب الفاعلة وغيرها. وكذلك من طريق الأولى أنه لم يكن ما هو هو أولى بأن يكون هو هو فليس ما ليس أولى فهو هذا. وأيضًا إن كان كل واحد منهما في ترتيب أكثر وأفضل فإنه إذا كان كل واحد منهما أكثر وأفضل من جميع الغير في ذلك الترتيب فهما واحد. وأما إذا كان أحدهما أكثر في ذلك من الآخر أو كان أكثر من كل ما سواه فليس أحدهما هو الآخر؛ ثمَّ من اللوازم أن يكون الترتيب واحدا. ومن المواضع أيضًا أن ينظر هل يختلف في الأقوال العارضة، وأيضًا هل يرتقي إلى مقولات مختلفة، وهل إن كان جنسها واحدًا ففصولها كذلك؛ وأمثال هذه المواضع مواضع الإبطال. وأيضًا هل كل واحد منهما إذا أضيف إلى ثالث يحصل مجموعا هو بعينه مجموع الآخر. وأيضًا هل يتساويان مما يلزم وضع الشيء ورفعه أو يلزمه رفع الشيء ووضعه كان ذلك حقا وباطلا؛ فإن الشرطية ليس صدقها في صدق المقدم أو التالي بل فيصدق اللزوم. ومثاله أنه إن كان الهواء والخلاء واحدًا فما يلزم من رفع الهواء كما يلزم من رفع الخلاء، وما يلزم من وضع الهواء يلزم من وضع الخلاء. وما يلزمه الهواء أو يلزم رفعه عند وضعه أو رفعه كذلك يلزمه الخلاء / أو رفعه لكنا إذا توهمنا رفع الهواء بقي الخلاء عند أصحاب الخلاء؛ وليس يلزم عند رفع الهواء أن يبقى وضع الخلاء فليس الهواء والخلاء واحدًا. وأيضًا هل يختلف الأمران في المحمولات؛ وهذا كالمكرَّر بالقوة وموضع في قوة هذا وهو إن لم يكونا واحدًا بالجنس إن كان لهما جنس ، أو لم يكونا واحدًا بالنوع إن كان لهما نوع لم يكونا واحدًا بالعدد بالوجه الذي مرَّ : وهذه المواضع كثير؛ منها مواضع الإثبات والإبطال المطلقين يستعمل في محمول مخصوص وهو الهو هو وكثير منها يخص الهو هو ؛ ويجب أن ننظر كي لا يكون أحدهما ليس محمولا على الآخر بما قدمناه من مواضع الإثبات والإبطال والتعرض لهذه المواضع التي مرَّ ذكرها كلا وجملة لأجل أنها مستعملة في القياس الجدلية وما يتعلق بها، ولنقتصر على هذا القدر فإن التعرُّض للزوائد من الزوائد وإن كانت لا يخلو من الفوائد.
Then among the loci are the loci of convertibility, as when justice is identical to courage; so the courageous person is just, and the just person is courageous, and conversely if the just person is identical to the courageous person. So courage is justice, and justice is courage. It differs from the loci in the category of accident, because there 'is it itself' is not required, but only predication. Similarly in the case of opposites, corruptions, efficient causes, and others. Also from the argument from superiority: if something is not more worthy of being 'is it itself', then what is not more worthy is not this. Also if each of them is in an ordering more and better, then if each of them is more and better than all others in that ordering, they are one. But if one of them is more in that than the other or is more than all else, then one of them is not the other. Then from the concomitants, the ordering must be one. Also among the loci is to consider whether they differ in accidental predications, and also whether they ascend to different categories, and whether if their genus is one their differentiate are also one; and such loci are loci of falsification. Also whether each of them, when added to a third, produces a sum identical to the sum of the other. Also whether they are equal in that positing the thing and removing it necessitate or its removal and positing necessitate, whether that is true or false; for the conditional's truth is not in the truth of the antecedent or consequent, but in the truth of the implication. An example: if air and void are one, then what follows from the removal of air follows as from the removal of void, and what follows from the positing of air follows from the positing of void. And what air necessitates or its removal necessitates upon its positing or removal, likewise void necessitates it or its removal. But if we imagine the removal of air, void remains according to proponents of the void; and it does not follow upon the removal of air that the positing of void remains, so air and void are not one. Also whether the two matters differ in attributes; and this is like a repeated potentiality and a locus 'in the power of this', and if they are not one in genus (if they have a genus), or not one in species (if they have a species), they are not one in number in the manner mentioned. These loci are many; among them are the loci of absolute affirmation and falsification used in a specific predicate, which is 'is it itself', and many of them pertain to 'is it itself'. And we must consider so that one of them is not predicated on the other by what we have previously mentioned from the loci of affirmation and falsification. And covering these loci mentioned generally and in detail is because they are used in dialectical syllogism and what pertains to it. And we will restrict ourselves to this amount, for engaging with superfluities is superfluous, though not devoid of benefits.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage is a classification of various loci (topics) used in dialectical reasoning to determine whether two things are identical ( هو هو ) or different. The author begins with the locus of convertibility (التصريف): if two attributes are identical in essence, then they are convertible; e.g., if justice is courage, then every just person is courageous and vice versa. This differs from accidental predication (باب العرض), where 'is it itself' is not required. The author then discusses the argument from superiority (من طريق الأولى): if one thing is not more worthy of being itself than another, they are not identical. Also, if two things are equally more and better in an ordering, they are one; otherwise not. Another locus involves consdering whether they have the same genus and differentiate; if not, they are different. The author gives an example using the hypothetical identity of air and void: if they were identical, the entailments of positing or removing one would match the other, but since removing air does not remove void (according to proponents of the void), they are not identical. The passage also mentions loci of comparison in terms of composition (adding to a third) and conditional entailment (اللزوم). Finally, the author notes that these loci are used in dialectical syllogisms and that only the essential ones are mentioned.

تصريف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the locus of convertibility from accidental predication?
A) Convertibility requires 'is it itself' whereas accident does not.
B) Accidental predication requires convertibility.
C) Both require the same kind of predication.
D) Convertibility only applies to substances.

Key Takeaway
The convertibility locus tests identity by checking whether two terms can be substituted salva veritate in predication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take two attributes from Islamic theology, e.g., al-ʿAlīm (the All-Knowing) and al-Qadīr (the All-Powerful). Construct a convertibility test: If they are identical, then 'every Knower is Powerful' and 'every Powerful is Knower' must hold. Evaluate whether this is plausible based on the Islamic concept of God.
